And those tools include all sorts of tie-breaking rules for resolving ambiguity even in the closest cases.  Courts manage to make do with these tools in many other areas of the law, so one might hope they will hardly ever find them inadequate here.  And if they do, they will now have to conduct a further inquiry that includes so few firm guides and so many cryptic "markers" that they will rarely, if ever, have to defer to an agency regulatory interpretation that differs from what they believe is the best and fairest reading.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But whatever happens, this case hardly promises to be this Court's last word on <em>Auer</em>.  If today's opinion ends up reducing <em>Auer</em> to the role of a tin god--officious, but ultimately powerless--then a future Court should candidly admit as much and stop requiring litigants and lower courts to pay token homage to it.  Alternatively, if <em>Auer</em> proves more resilient, this Court should reassert its responsibility to say what the law is and afford the people the neutral forum for their disputes that they expect and deserve.</p>
<p></p><hr>





<p align="CENTER"><span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Kavanaugh, J.</small></span>, concurring in judgment</p>
<p align="CENTER"> 588 U.&nbsp;S. ____ (2019)</p>


<p align="CENTER">No. 18-15</p>


<center><h2><p align="CENTER">james l. kisor, PETITIONER <em>v. </em>ROBERT WILKIE, SECRETARY OF VETERANS AFFAIRS</p>
</h2></center><center><h4><p align="CENTER"><span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>on writ of certiorari to the united states court of appeals for the federal circuit</small></span></p>
</h4></center><center><p align="CENTER">[June 26, 2019]</p>
</center><p></p><hr>

<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Justice Kavanaugh</small></span>, with whom <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Justice Alito</small></span> joins, concurring in the judgment.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I agree with <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Justice Gorsuch</small></span>'s conclusion that the <em>Auer </em>deference doctrine should be formally retired.  I write separately to emphasize two points.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<em>First</em>, I agree with <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>The Chief Justice</small></span> that "the distance between the majority and <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Justice Gorsuch</small></span> is not as great as it may initially appear."  <em>Ante,</em> at 1 (opinion concurring in part).  The majority's approach in Part II−B of its opinion closely resembles the argument advanced by the Solicitor General to "clarif[y] and narro[w]" <em>Auer</em>.  Brief for Respondent 15.  Importantly, the majority borrows from footnote 9 of this Court's opinion in <em>Chevron </em>to say that a reviewing court must "exhaust all the 'traditional tools' of construction" before concluding that an agency rule is ambiguous and deferring to an agency's reasonable interpretation.  <em>Ante, </em>at 14 (quoting <em>Chevron U.&nbsp;S.&nbsp;A. Inc.</em> v. <em>Natural Resources Defense Council, Inc.</em>, 467 U.&nbsp;S. 837, 843, n. 9 (1984)).  If a reviewing court employs all of the traditional tools of construction, the court will almost always reach a conclusion about the best interpretation of the regulation at issue.  After doing so, the court then will have no need to adopt or defer to an agency's contrary interpretation.  In other words, the footnote 9 principle, taken seriously, means that courts will have no reason or basis to put a thumb on the scale in favor of an agency when courts interpret agency regulations.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Formally rejecting <em>Auer</em> would have been a more direct approach, but rigorously applying footnote 9 should lead in most cases to the same general destination.  Umpires in games at Wrigley Field do not defer to the Cubs manager's in-game interpretation of Wrigley's ground rules.  So too here.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To be sure, some cases involve regulations that employ broad and open-ended terms like "reasonable," "appropriate," "feasible," or "practicable."  Those kinds of terms afford agencies broad policy discretion, and courts allow an agency to reasonably exercise its discretion to choose among the options allowed by the text of the rule.  But that is more <em>State Farm </em>than <em>Auer</em>.  See <em>Motor Vehicle Mfrs. Assn. of United States, Inc.</em> v. <em>State Farm Mut. Automobile Ins. Co.</em>, 463 U.&nbsp;S. 29 (1983).</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In short, after today's decision, a judge should engage in appropriately rigorous scrutiny of an agency's interpretation of a regulation, and can simultaneously be appropriately deferential to an agency's reasonable policy choices within the discretion allowed by a regulation.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<em>Second</em>, I also agree with <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>The Chief Justice</small></span> that "[i]ssues surrounding judicial deference to agency interpretations of their own regulations are distinct from those raised in connection with judicial deference to agency interpretations of statutes enacted by Congress."  <em>Ante, </em>at 2.  Like <span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>The Chief Justice</small></span>, "I do not regard the Court's decision" not to formally overrule <em>Auer "</em>to touch upon the latter question."  <em>Ibid.</em></p>
<p></p><hr>


<br><h3>FOOTNOTES</h3>
<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 1" name="FNopinion1.1" href="#FRopinion1.1">1</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;In case you're wondering, the regulatory definition of active moiety is "[t]he molecule or ion, excluding those appended portions of the molecule that cause the drug to be an ester, salt (including a salt with hydrogen or coordination bonds), or the noncovalent derivative (such as a complex, chelate, or clathrate) of the molecule, responsible for the physiological or pharmacological action of the drug substance."  21 CFR §314.3(b) (2018).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 2" name="FNopinion1.2" href="#FRopinion1.2">2</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See, <em>e.g.</em>, <em>PLIVA, Inc.</em> v. <em>Mensing</em>, 564 U.&nbsp;S. 604, 613 (2011); <em>Chase Bank USA, N. A. </em>v. <em>McCoy</em>, 562 U.&nbsp;S. 195, 208-210 (2011); <em>Coeur Alaska, Inc.</em> v. <em>Southeast Alaska Conservation Council</em>, 557 U.&nbsp;S. 261, 274-275 (2009); <em>Riegel</em> v. <em>Medtronic, Inc.</em>, 552 U.&nbsp;S. 312, 328 (2008); <em>Long Island Care at Home, Ltd.</em> v. <em>Coke</em>, 551 U.&nbsp;S. 158, 171 (2007); <em>Washington State Dept. of Social and Health Servs.</em> v. <em>Guardianship Estate of Keffeler</em>, 537 U.&nbsp;S. 371, 387-388 (2003).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 3" name="FNopinion1.3" href="#FRopinion1.3">3</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Our (pre-<em>Auer</em>)<em> </em>decisions applying <em>Seminole Rock </em>deference are legion.  See, <em>e.g.</em>, <em>Shalala</em> v. <em>Guernsey Memorial Hospital</em>, 514 U.&nbsp;S. 87, 94-95 (1995); <em>Thomas Jefferson Univ</em>. v. <em>Shalala</em>, 512 U.&nbsp;S. 504, 512 (1994); <em>Stinson</em> v. <em>United States</em>, 508 U.&nbsp;S. 36, 44-45 (1993); <em>INS</em> v. <em>National Center for Immigrants' Rights, Inc.</em>, 502 U.&nbsp;S. 183, 189-190 (1991); <em>Robertson</em> v. <em>Methow Valley Citizens Council</em>, 490 U.&nbsp;S. 332, 358-359 (1989); <em>Mullins Coal Co. of Va.</em> v. <em>Director, Office of Workers' Compensation Programs</em>, 484 U.&nbsp;S. 135, 159 (1987); <em>Lyng</em> v. <em>Payne</em>, 476 U.&nbsp;S. 926, 939 (1986); <em>Fidelity Fed. Sav. &amp; Loan Assn.</em> v. <em>De la Cuesta</em>, 458 U.&nbsp;S. 141, 158, n.&nbsp;13 (1982); <em>Blanding</em> v. <em>DuBose</em>, 454 U.&nbsp;S. 393, 401 (1982) (<em>per curiam</em>); <em>Ford Motor Credit Co.</em> v. <em>Milhollin</em>, 444 U.&nbsp;S. 555, 566 (1980); <em>United States</em> v. <em>Larionoff</em>, 431 U.&nbsp;S. 864, 872 (1977); <em>Northern Indiana Public Service Co.</em> v. <em>Porter County Chapter of Izaak Walton League of America, Inc.</em>, 423 U.&nbsp;S. 12, 15 (1975) (<em>per curiam</em>); <em>Ehlert</em> v. <em>United States</em>, 402 U. S. 99, 105 (1971); <em>INS </em>v.<em> Stanisic</em>, 395 U.&nbsp;S. 62, 72 (1969); <em>Thorpe</em> v. <em>Housing Authority of Durham</em>, 393 U.&nbsp;S. 268, 276 (1969); <em>Udall</em> v. <em>Tallman</em>, 380 U.&nbsp;S. 1, 16-17 (1965).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 4" name="FNopinion1.4" href="#FRopinion1.4">4</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;The proper understanding of the scope and limits of the <em>Auer</em> doctrine is, of course, not set out in any of the opinions that concur only in the judgment.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 5" name="FNopinion1.5" href="#FRopinion1.5">5</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;For a similar reason, this Court has denied <em>Auer </em>deference when an agency interprets a rule that parrots the statutory text.  See <em>Gonzales</em> v. <em>Oregon</em>, 546 U. S. 243, 257 (2006).  An agency, we explained, gets no "special authority to interpret its own words when, instead of using its expertise and experience to formulate a regulation, it has elected merely to paraphrase the statutory language."  <em>Ibid.</em></p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 6" name="FNopinion1.6" href="#FRopinion1.6">6</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;The general rule, then, is not to give deference to agency interpretations advanced for the first time in legal briefs.  See <em>Bowen</em>, 488 U.&nbsp;S., at 212-213.  But we have not entirely foreclosed that practice.  <em>Auer </em>itself deferred to a new regulatory interpretation presented in an <em>amicus curiae</em> brief in this Court.  There, the agency was not a party to the litigation, and had expressed its views only in response to the Court's request.  "[I]n the circumstances," the Court explained, "[t]here [was] simply no reason to suspect that the interpretation [did] not reflect the agency's fair and considered judgment on the matter in question."  <em>Auer</em>, 519 U.&nbsp;S., at 462.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 47" name="FNopinion1.47" href="#FRopinion1.47">47</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;The case before us doesn't arise under the APA, but the statute that governs here is plainly modeled on the APA and contains essentially the same commands.  It directs a reviewing court to "decide all relevant questions of law" and to "set aside any regulation or any interpretation thereof&nbsp;" that is "not in accordance with law."  38 U.&nbsp;S.&nbsp;C. §7292(d)(1).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 48" name="FNopinion1.48" href="#FRopinion1.48">48</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See, <em>e.g.</em>, §706(2)(A) (arbitrary and capricious, abuse of discretion); §706(2)(E) (substantial evidence); see also <em>Universal Camera Corp.</em> v. <em>NLRB</em>, 340 U.&nbsp;S. 474, 482, n.&nbsp;14 (1951) (noting that as originally proposed, the APA's judicial review provision would have included an explicit requirement for courts to accord "due weight" to "the experience, technical competence, specialized knowledge, and legislative policy of the agency involved as well as the discretionary authority conferred upon it" (internal quotation marks omitted)).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 101" name="FNopinion1.101" href="#FRopinion1.101">101</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Ibid.</em></p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 102" name="FNopinion1.102" href="#FRopinion1.102">102</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See Criddle &amp; Staszewski, Against Methodological Stare Decisis, 102 Geo. L.&nbsp;J. 1573, 1577, and n.&nbsp;12 (2014); C. Oldfather, Methodological Stare Decisis and Constitutional Interpretation, in Precedent in the United States Supreme Court 135, 135-136 (C. Peters ed. 2013).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 103" name="FNopinion1.103" href="#FRopinion1.103">103</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Kozel, Statutory Interpretation, Administrative Deference, and the Law of Stare Decisis, 97 Texas L.&nbsp;Rev. 1125, 1159 (2019); see Raso &amp; Eskridge, <em>Chevron</em> as a Canon, Not a Precedent: An Empirical Study of What Motivates Justices in Agency Deference Cases, 110 Colum. L.&nbsp;Rev. 1727, 1765-1766 (2010) (concluding that in practice, this Court has not treated administrative-deference regimes such as <em>Chevron</em> and <em>Auer</em> as binding precedents).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 104" name="FNopinion1.104" href="#FRopinion1.104">104</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>South Dakota</em> v. <em>Wayfair</em>,<em> Inc.</em>, 585 U.&nbsp;S. ___, ___ (2018) (slip op., at 18).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 105" name="FNopinion1.105" href="#FRopinion1.105">105</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See, <em>e.g.</em>, Alexander &amp; Prakash, Mother May I?  Imposing Mandatory Prospective Rules of Statutory Interpretation, 20 Const. Comment. 97 (2003); Elhauge, Preference-Estimating Statutory Default Rules, 102 Colum. L.&nbsp;Rev. 2027, 2109-2110, and nn.&nbsp;231-233 (2002).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 106" name="FNopinion1.106" href="#FRopinion1.106">106</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Pearson</em> v. <em>Callahan</em>, 555 U.&nbsp;S. 223, 233 (2009).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 107" name="FNopinion1.107" href="#FRopinion1.107">107</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Arizona</em> v. <em>Gant</em>, 556 U.&nbsp;S. 332, 348 (2009) (quoting <em>Lawrence</em> v. <em>Texas</em>, 539 U.&nbsp;S. 558, 577 (2003)).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 108" name="FNopinion1.108" href="#FRopinion1.108">108</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Janus </em>v. <em>State</em>,<em> County</em>,<em> and Municipal Employees</em>, 585 U.&nbsp;S. ___, ___-___ (2018) (slip op., at 34-35).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 109" name="FNopinion1.109" href="#FRopinion1.109">109</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Brief for Administrative Law Scholars as <em>Amici Curiae</em> 13.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 110" name="FNopinion1.110" href="#FRopinion1.110">110</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Knick</em> v. <em>Township of Scott</em>, <em>ante</em>, at 22; see <em>Janus</em>, 585 U.&nbsp;S., at ___ (slip op., at 23).  See also Lost History 54-92; Knudsen &amp; Wildermuth, 22 Geo. Mason L.&nbsp;Rev., at 658-664.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 111" name="FNopinion1.111" href="#FRopinion1.111">111</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Hickman &amp; Thomson, 103 Minn. L.&nbsp;Rev. Headnotes, at 110.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 112" name="FNopinion1.112" href="#FRopinion1.112">112</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Green</em> v. <em>Brennan</em>, 578 U.&nbsp;S. ___, ___ (2016) (slip op., at 5); see, <em>e.g.</em>,<strong> </strong><em>National Assn. of Home Builders</em> v. <em>Defenders of Wildlife</em>, 551 U.&nbsp;S. 644, 668-669 (2007) (construing regulation in light of text, history, and canon against surplusage).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 113" name="FNopinion1.113" href="#FRopinion1.113">113</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Woods</em>, 571 U.&nbsp;S., at 48; see also <em>Bruesewitz</em> v. <em>Wyeth LLC</em>, 562 U.&nbsp;S. 223, 242 (2011); <em>Jones</em> v. <em>United States</em>, 526 U.&nbsp;S. 227, 238 (1999); <em>United States</em> v. <em>Mine Workers</em>, 330 U.&nbsp;S. 258, 281-282 (1947).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 114" name="FNopinion1.114" href="#FRopinion1.114">114</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;To be sure, under <em>Chevron U.&nbsp;S.&nbsp;A. Inc.</em> v. <em>Natural Resources Defense Council</em>,<em> Inc.</em>, 467 U.&nbsp;S. 837 (1984), we sometimes defer to an agency's construction of a <em>statute</em>.  But there are serious questions, too, about whether <em>that</em> doctrine comports with the APA and the Constitution.  See, <em>e.g.</em>, <em>Pereira</em> v. <em>Sessions</em>, 585 U.&nbsp;S. ___, ___-___ (2018) (Kennedy, J., concurring); <em>Michigan</em> v. <em>EPA</em>, 576 U.&nbsp;S. ___, ___-___ (2015) (<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Thomas</small></span>, J., concurring); <em>Perez</em>, 575 U.&nbsp;S., at ___-___ (Scalia, J., concurring in judgment) (slip op., at 2-3).  Regardless, it would be a mistake to suppose that <em>Auer</em> is in any way a "logical corollary to <em>Chevron</em>."  <em>Decker</em>, 568 U.&nbsp;S., at 620 (Scalia, J., concurring in part and dissenting in part).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 115" name="FNopinion1.115" href="#FRopinion1.115">115</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Arlington</em>, 569 U.&nbsp;S., at 313 (<span style="text-transform: uppercase;"><small>Roberts</small></span>, C.&nbsp;J., dissenting) (internal quotation marks omitted).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 116" name="FNopinion1.116" href="#FRopinion1.116">116</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Federal Maritime Comm'n</em> v. <em>South Carolina Ports Authority</em>, 535 U.&nbsp;S. 743, 755 (2002).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 117" name="FNopinion1.117" href="#FRopinion1.117">117</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See Office of the Federal Register, Code of Federal Regulations: Total Pages 1938-1949, and Total Volumes and Pages 1950-2018, http://www.federalregister.gov/uploads/2019/04/cfrTotalPages2018.pdf; <em>United States</em> v. <em>Secretary</em>,<em> Fla. Dept. of Corrections</em>, 778 F.&nbsp;3d 1223, 1225 (CA11 2015).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 118" name="FNopinion1.118" href="#FRopinion1.118">118</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Janus</em>, 585 U.&nbsp;S., at ___ (slip op., at 45) (quoting <em>Gant</em>, 556 U.&nbsp;S., at 349).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 119" name="FNopinion1.119" href="#FRopinion1.119">119</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Gonzales</em> v. <em>Oregon</em>, 546 U.&nbsp;S. 243, 269 (2006); see <em>Christopher</em>, 567 U.&nbsp;S., at 159 (applying <em>Skidmore</em> after concluding that agency's interpretation did not merit <em>Auer</em> deference).</p>
 
        <p></p>

        <p class="case-information__paragraph"><b class="case-information__paragraph-topic">Decided:</b> June 26, 2019</p>
        <p class="case-information__paragraph"><b class="case-information__paragraph-topic">Court:</b> United States Supreme Court</p>

    </footer><script>_satellite["_runScript1"](function(event, target, Promise) {
_satellite.ads = {};

_satellite.ads.adInfoFactory = function(nameString, href) {
  // TODO remove this once the correct PA is being used for the lid
  if( _satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context') && _satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context').pa ) {
    nameString = nameString.replace(/pa:[0-9]+/, "pa:"+_satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context').pa);  
  }
  _satellite.logger.debug('_satellite.ads.adInfoFactory nameString: '+nameString);

  // sample name: "&lid=clk:fs/prod:dts/cid:5088127/msa:259/pa:1313/sub:3107462/pos:1"
  var s = nameString;
  s = s.substr(5);
  var lid = s;
  s = s.replaceAll(':','":"');
  s = s.replaceAll('/','","');
  s = '{"'+s+'"}'
  var adInfo = JSON.parse(s);
  adInfo.lid = lid;
  adInfo.paid = (typeof adInfo.sub != 'undefined');
  adInfo.adId = (adInfo.paid ? adInfo.sub : adInfo.cid);
  var map = {
    'ph':'phone',
    'fs':'website',
    'pv':'profile',
    'cu':'contact',
    'vr':'review-read',
    'wr':'review-write',
    'sl':'super-lawyers'
  };  
  adInfo.type = map[adInfo.clk];   
  adInfo.transactionId = _satellite.getVar('fl_user_id')+'-'+adInfo.adId+'-'+(new Date().getTime());
  
  if( href && adInfo.type == 'phone' ) {
    adInfo.detail = href.replace(/[^\d]/g,'');
    if( adInfo.detail.length > 10 ) {
      adInfo.detail = adInfo.detail.substr(adInfo.detail.length-10);
    }
  }  
  
  return adInfo;
}

_satellite.ads.trackAdEngagement = function(adInfo) {
  if( typeof adInfo.adId == 'undefined' ) {
    return false;
  }
  if( typeof FLDataLayer.ads == 'undefined' ) {
    FLDataLayer.ads = {};
  }
  if( typeof FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements == 'undefined' ) {
    FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements = [];
  }
  for( var i=0; i < FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements.length; i++ ) {
    if( FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements[i].type == adInfo.type && FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements[i].adId == adInfo.adId ) {
      return true;
    }
  }

  FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements.push(adInfo);
  return false;
}

_satellite.ads.sendConversionFindLaw = function() {

  // we use a cookie to ensure multiple beacons are not sent for the same ad
  if( typeof c == 'undefined' ) {
    _satellite.setFlCookie(cookieName, cookieValue, 1);

    var data = {};
    var clickUrlElement = document.getElementById(_satellite.getVar('ad_eng_sub'));
    if (clickUrlElement !== null) {
      data.clickUrl = clickUrlElement.innerText;
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context') ) {
      data.adDecisionContext = _satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context');
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('ad_eng_transaction_id') ) {
      data.transactionId = _satellite.getVar('ad_eng_transaction_id');
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('ad_eng_sub') ) {
      data.subId = _satellite.getVar('ad_eng_sub');
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('fl_user_id') ) {
      data.flUserId = _satellite.getVar('fl_user_id');
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('fl_tag_track') == 'false' ) {
      data.internalFlag = 'true'; // mimick as an internal request
    }

    let url = new URL(window.location.href);
    let domain = 'attorneys.findlaw'+(_satellite.getVar('cms_env') == 'prod' ? '' : '-stage')+'.com';
    let attorneysUrl = new URL('https://'+domain+'/flstats/v1/stats');
    let searchParams = new URLSearchParams(window.location.search);

    if (searchParams.has('ads-server-env')) {
      attorneysUrl.searchParams.set('ads-server-env', url.searchParams.get('ads-server-env'));
    }
    navigator.sendBeacon(attorneysUrl.href, JSON.stringify(data));
  }
}

function setTrackerCookie(name, value)
{
  var hostParts = location.host.split('.').reverse();
  var cookieDomain = '.' + hostParts[1] + '.' + hostParts[0];
  document.cookie = name + '=' + value + ';domain=' + cookieDomain + ';path=/';
}
